  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c0456e62-b9ca-4793-9b48-b7f811472780'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer7540472439162132892">Galaxy “Alex” Stern is the most unlikely member of Yale’s freshman class. Raised in the Los Angeles hinterlands by a hippie mom, Alex dropped out of school early and into a world of shady drug dealer boyfriends, dead-end jobs, and much, much worse. By age twenty, in fact, she is the sole survivor of a horrific, unsolved multiple homicide. Some might say she’s thrown her li</span>
  <span id="freeText7540472439162132892" style="display:none">Galaxy “Alex” Stern is the most unlikely member of Yale’s freshman class. Raised in the Los Angeles hinterlands by a hippie mom, Alex dropped out of school early and into a world of shady drug dealer boyfriends, dead-end jobs, and much, much worse. By age twenty, in fact, she is the sole survivor of a horrific, unsolved multiple homicide. Some might say she’s thrown her life away. But at her hospital bed, Alex is offered a second chance: to attend one of the world’s most elite universities on a full ride. What’s the catch, and why her?<br /><br />Still searching for answers to this herself, Alex arrives in New Haven tasked by her mysterious benefactors with monitoring the activities of Yale’s secret societies. These eight windowless “tombs” are well-known to be haunts of the future rich and powerful, from high-ranking politicos to Wall Street and Hollywood’s biggest players. But their occult activities are revealed to be more sinister and more extraordinary than any paranoid imagination might conceive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7540472439162132892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    The scene is basically from pages 122-124 from Chapter 7, however I think it's also referenced or reflected on later in the book. There's also a bunch<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    The scene is basically from pages 122-124 from Chapter 7, however I think it's also referenced or reflected on later in the book. There's also a bunch of other content warnings (including sexual assault) so I would proceed with caution if you feel any of them could be harmful to you. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_2492981005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492981005" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492981005?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473227965" href="/book/show/44140764-ninth-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-sff">adult-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492981005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8282452352948692401">I picked up this book with a mad feeling of hope flooding my limbs. The premise promised me an entry to what I now consider to be my favorite genre—namely, novels that initiate their readers from the outset into a secret club, hidden from everyone else, the way an oyster conceals the pearl at its heart, which is probably what every good novel should do. I couldn’t imagine anyone in a better position to deliver this story than the author I believe to be one of the finest in her field.<br/><br/><strong>But what a s</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText8282452352948692401" style="display:none">I picked up this book with a mad feeling of hope flooding my limbs. The premise promised me an entry to what I now consider to be my favorite genre—namely, novels that initiate their readers from the outset into a secret club, hidden from everyone else, the way an oyster conceals the pearl at its heart, which is probably what every good novel should do. I couldn’t imagine anyone in a better position to deliver this story than the author I believe to be one of the finest in her field.<br /><br /><strong>But what a slim hope to rest my heart upon.</strong><br /><br />In Leigh Bardugo’s first offering to the adult genre, Yale University wears claws hidden in a velvet glove. Here where magic didn’t require skill so much as a steady lavishing of grotesqueries, and men in power used their loyalty to underground societies to further their own ambitions, eager to commit their weight to the great lever and move the world—without counting the cost.<br /><br />Peering down from a lofty chair at the rest of the societies was <b>House of Lethe</b>, standing guard to ensure that their unwholesome affairs won’t tip them into a whirling chaos that could eat them whole. To this end, Lethe needed someone who could see ghosts. <b>Galaxy Stern trailed an army of ghosts that only she could see.</b> They were a matchmaker’s dream.<br /><br />Alex is recruited with all the boorish self-interest of a rich man purchasing a racehorse, and given a chance to scrub her past clean like a chemical burn. Alex clings to it like a drowning woman offered a buoy, even when ordered to follow at Darlington’s heels like an obedient hound. <b>Daniel “Darlington” Arlington</b> is as inerrant in his presence as he is with his duty to Lethe. Alex’s lies are adequate, but Darlington’s gaze, fastened on her, is a mirror that granted a ruinous glimpse of herself, and it spoke of abandon and fearlessness, a person dangerously unmoored from their own future.<br /><br />Now there is a fog creeping along at their heels, swallowing their footsteps and erasing their evidence, and when a girl winds up dead and Darlington melts to nothing before Alex’s eyes, the wrongness of what they’re doing hangs like gun smoke in the air. Darlington believed they were safe in Lethe—they were the <em>shepherds</em>, after all—but Lethe only bestows the kind of protection that weighs and measures before it finds you worthy. The societies will always have a comfortable veil of money between them and the rest of the world, but Alex knows that when the deal she made falls through she would be shuffled to the side, abandoned, cut off and once again powerless. <br /><br />Luckily, survival is a blade she’d honed to a hair’s edge, and Alex is well versed in the art of dodging and scheming up until the very moment of flipping the car and crashing in flames.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Mors irrumat omnia. Death fucks us all.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I kept asking myself, while reading, how it could be that I was so decidedly not enjoying a book that was so perfectly calculated to be my literary ideal, and here, I think, is the answer.<br /><br />Bardugo has always been good at fully bringing to life a place most couldn’t pretend to know, and has already displayed a great gift for plot in her YA Grishaverse books, but I was left craving the vividly and mordantly splendid story lines we know she’s capable of delivering. Despite its flashes of poignant beauty—there is a recurrent scene from this book that surfaces in my mind again and again, like an obsessive undercurrent in a dream: Alex standing, like a temple icon to an evil goddess, (“<em>night ebbed and flowed around her in a cape of glittering stars</em>”), and Darlington with a sword in his back that felled him to his knees, to <em>her</em> mercy, his plea of “<em>Choose m</em>e” a frantic, unspoken chant—<em>Ninth</em> <em>House’s</em> blend of the mundane and the magical did not tip far enough to the latter for me.<br /><br />Bardugo favors detailed explication over keeping a steady pace, and it’s problematic when the flow of the story is hampered by its slow build and lack of major plot movement. Some naive corner of my mind kept holding its breath in expectation, but my initial excitement soon slipped away, and hope fell shortly on its heels. Though the back-and-forth structure eventually takes on a deeper resonance as more secrets are gradually unearthed, I’m not sure it’s enough to forgive. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“We all have spaces we keep blank.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>Ninth House</em> is indeed not for the squeamish. Then again, it's hard to imagine anyone whose mind won’t recoil from it, whose soul won’t curdle reading it. That said, it isn’t the grimmest, or bleakest book I’ve ever read. In fact, Bardugo sometimes tries too hard for big, dramatic horror, and the violence comes off as gratuitous, her ghosts sometimes too chain-rattling to believe. I was deeply (and, as it turned out, accurately) concerned that some themes would not be handled with enough conscious sensibility woven into the fabric of the story, and would instead be dolloped on top to serve for shock value. <em>Ninth House</em> is about all kinds of trauma, yet I found that the consequences of such a monumental thing are barely brushed upon. The novel is rife with flashbacks, seen through Alex’s eyes as she passively witnesses the horrifying events of her past, but her trauma-suppressed memories seemingly only resurface whenever it's convenient for the plot, and without much of a statement being made besides. And that occasionally struck a sour note.<br /><br />Ultimately, this is the novel’s biggest misstep for me—that it curiously avoids fully engaging with the meat of its themes. At points in <em>Ninth House</em>, it seems that Bardugo is setting herself up to make a deep point about privilege and power—mystical, emotional, institutional—and what happens when it's abused, even in small, quiet ways, but nothing satisfying comes of that tantalizing notion. And though the driving force of the narrative is a classic whodunit, with Bardugo structuring the book like a detective yarn of sorts, I don't know whether it works like a crime novel; Alex is sharp, frail she was, yet crafty, but the narrative may hand her a few too many gifts.<br /><br />The emotional register of <em>Ninth House</em>, too, is of a different order from either of Bardugo’s previous works—for me, at least. I don’t feel like the novel managed to pierce the veil that separates the reader from the human puzzle pieces on the page. Alex is a difficult character to like—no matter how much I tried to put my arms around her, I might as well have embraced an oak. I found her largely stiff and drab, one of those characters that are so passive and colorless that you wonder why all these intriguing people don't ditch them and hang out with each other instead. There’s a roaring vitality to her that’s always just beneath the surface, though, and I wanted to poke at it until it gave way to something more.<br /><br />Despite having considerably less page-time, Darlington’s character, on the other hand, manages to shine amid a constant barrage of wonders and grotesqueries. There’s an embodied presence to him, depth and information—and it kept me riveted throughout.<br /><br />Darlington lived with an endless commotion inside, and the part of him that sought danger, like an ember sought air, fit in with Lethe like a bolt sliding into place. He was the boy who was permanently discontent with the ordinary and convinced of the existence of the extraordinary. The boy who hasn’t yet lost the unbruised part of himself that <em>believed </em>in magic with a fervor that strayed perilously close to mortification. And as gruesomely and cruelly as the game was stacked, Darlington always played it with a kind of mystic joy, even when it convulsed around him. You could not parse the idea of beauty being attributed to anyone or anything consigned to such a horrid world, yet it was always embellished in Darlington’s mind. Because he was relieved to have done it, to finally be inside the magic instead of looking at it through a window—even when that magic was ready to claw and tore at him.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>That was what magic did. It revealed the heart of who you’d been before life took away your belief in the possible. It gave back the world all lonely children longed for. That was what Lethe had done for him. Maybe it could do that for Alex as well.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Overall, I think <em>Ninth House</em> inches in many intriguing directions, but unfortunately, it's not enough to enliven such a tepid outing. But I'll be reading the next installment just for more glimpses of Darlington.<br /><br /><b>Trigger Warnings (courtesy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/77786613-roe" rel="nofollow noopener">Roe</a>):</b> rape of a child, sexual assault under influence of a magical drug, drowning, heavy violence, gore, drug addiction, overdosing, death, suicide, blackmail, self-harm, and forced consumption of human waste.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8282452352948692401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2343881211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343881211" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343881211?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=book-expo-2019">book-expo-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343881211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3249349267466162323"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560360462i/27658277._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC acquired at <a href='https://youtu.be/27bxzSm9lq8' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Expo</a> in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There were always excuses for why girls died.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Ninth House</i> is a love letter to living and surviving unspeakable abuse. This is a book all about trauma, and PTSD, and healing, in any and every way that you can. This is a book for victims, who have felt they will never get the piece of them back that someone forcefully took. This is a book for anyone who was willing to do anything to feel empowered after something horrible occu</span>
  <span id="freeText3249349267466162323" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560360462i/27658277._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC acquired at <a href="https://youtu.be/27bxzSm9lq8" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Expo</a> in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There were always excuses for why girls died.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Ninth House</i> is a love letter to living and surviving unspeakable abuse. This is a book all about trauma, and PTSD, and healing, in any and every way that you can. This is a book for victims, who have felt they will never get the piece of them back that someone forcefully took. This is a book for anyone who was willing to do anything to feel empowered after something horrible occurred. This is a book about the dark and the light and the in between phases a human can go through to get their voice back.<br><br>But this is also a story about a girl named Galaxy Stern, or Alex, who is from LA, but is now across the country and studying at Yale. The book continuously switches back and forth from Late Spring to Winter, so we get to see what happened in the past and the ramifications it causes for present day Alex.<br><br>In the Winter, we get to see her starting Yale, meeting a man named Darlington, and learning all about the nine secret societies at Yale, with secret, magical rituals that they perform. Lethe recruits a new freshman every three years to join sixteen seniors every year, where they gain knowledge of the occult. And Alex was picked because she has a very sought-after ability, that she has been running from her entire life. Also, it is Lethe House’s responsibility as the ninth house to keep the others in order and make sure they aren’t doing bad things.<br><br>In the Spring, everything is different, and Alex is struggling with the weight of so much. From missing people, to ghosts who are paying her too much attention, to a girl being murdered that Alex can’t help but think was because of one of the secret societies, and she is willing to do anything to solve the case. Even if that means making a deal with one of the ghosts she is supposed to be ignoring.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But the trouble had begun on a night in the full dark of winter, when Tara Hutchins died and Alex still thought she might get away with everything.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Sounds pretty amazing, right? And I’m telling you, this book’s atmosphere, along with the campus setting, it was a perfect combination. Also, you all know that I think Leigh’s writing is a tier above most. The quotes I was able to pull from this book? They take the breath from my lungs even upon rereading them.<br><br>Also, this book has a beautiful discussion about privilege and power dynamics. Leigh does not hold back truth of what white, rich, privileged boys and how they feel they are entitled to any and everything, and God bless her for that. Cycles of abuse and entitlement truly can be passed down, leaving terrible things in their wake, which will impact so many victims for their entire lives. Unchecked privilege is a terrifying thing, friends. And Leigh is not scared to go there, in the terrible acts they commit, to the horrible ends they deserve, and I really appreciated it, and it may have been my favorite element of this book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Beautiful boys who should be happy, who wanted for nothing but still found things to take.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But you all are probably wondering why I gave this book three stars. I’m going to be brutally honest, not much happened in this book, and surely enough didn’t happen for this book to be almost 500 pages. I feel like you could easily cut this book in half and it would have been way more impactful and way more exciting to read. As much as I loved the healing of this book, and I loved the premise of secret societies all about the occult, I just felt so damn bored by reading this book. It started to feel like a chore to pick up, and this book took me twice the amount of time it would normally take me to read.<br><br>It also started to feel so formulaic, where something really bad and heartbreaking would happen (past or present) then we’d have 50+ pages of nothing, and then something even worse happens, then 50+ of nothing. I will never lessen anyone’s trauma or how they choose to write and heal about it, but this book just made me feel nothing and then immeasurably uncomfortably and sadness, back to back to back, and it made for a really not great reading experience for me. Also, my favorite character was for sure Darlington, and I really wish we could have seen so much more of him. And lastly, the ending sort of wrapped this story up, I guess? But it just left me desiring so much more, and not in a good way if I’m being honest.<br><br>So, let’s talk about the elephant in the room. I picked this book up the day before twitter exploded about the trigger warnings. I will be honest, it made for such a strange reading experience, because I felt like everyone was looking at me, even though I was only 100 pages into this book. At the end of this review, like always, I will have all the trigger warnings that I found listed. This is a dark book, with very dark themes and elements, and some extremely dark scenes. Alex truly has horrible things happen to her and her loved ones throughout her short life. I highly recommend you make sure you are in a safe headspace before picking this one up, because a few of these triggers are not my own, but they still really bothered me to read.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People didn’t need magic to be terrible to each other.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, this was a disappointment for me. This was easily my most anticipated release of 2019, besides <i>Queen of Nothing</i>, and maybe I just put it on a pedestal subconsciously. I do think this one will be polarizing upon release, and I have friends who love this more than me and dislike this more than me. Honestly, I’m in this weird middle ground where I loved the setting and atmosphere, but I didn’t love the story or characters. I will probably still pick up the next installment, I think I’m just going to go into it with lower expectations.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> drug use, overdosing, murder, death, loss of a loved one, rituals, gore, PTSD depiction, grief depiction, self-harm, bloodletting, rape, child (12) rape (it is only two pages, but it is very graphic), statutory rape (15), sexual assault, forced sexual assault on video, talk of suicide, blackmail, physical abuse, a magical date rape drug, forced eating of human waste (to a rapist), and racism (always in a negative light).</span>
  <a data-text-id="3249349267466162323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2661203342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2661203342" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2661203342?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2661203342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2617472548385414234">Yesssss! I finished this book in one hour and got all references at one time. I turned into most intelligent book reading machine and started to turn two pages at a time (because my mind can already feel what’s written at the next page, unbelievable, isn’t it?) I didn’t get bored. I didn’t yawn or complain about my heavy eyelids because I was so alert and concentrated. And of course, I loved those characters so much, I never had an urge to slap one of them or hate any of them. They were memorabl</span>
  <span id="freeText2617472548385414234" style="display:none">Yesssss! I finished this book in one hour and got all references at one time. I turned into most intelligent book reading machine and started to turn two pages at a time (because my mind can already feel what’s written at the next page, unbelievable, isn’t it?) I didn’t get bored. I didn’t yawn or complain about my heavy eyelids because I was so alert and concentrated. And of course, I loved those characters so much, I never had an urge to slap one of them or hate any of them. They were memorable, amazing, marvelous and fantastic!<br /><br />So after finishing this book, I went my culinary class and all of the students clapped me because I cooked an amazing soufflé, macaroons and paella in only 20 minutes.<br />Then I got a phone call from my husband suggested me to move to France and as a surprise he bought me a vineyard so we can raise our own grapes and produce our own wines! whaaaattt? <br /><br />And at home Netflix CEO and Martin Scorsese were waiting for me, playing with dogs, drinking my Chardonnay! They bended on their knees and begged me to work with them as my neighbors giving me a trophy for being “the most honorable and loveable neighbor of the city”! COME AGAIN???!<br /><br />Then I heard a voice and realized Tom Ellis standing in our living room, asking me: “Tell me, what is that you truly desire?” Yesssss!!!<br /><br />THEN I SUDDENLY WOKE UP! <br /><br /><br />Oh Come on, Martie and Lucifer Morningstar weren’t at my house! Damn it!<br /><br />Do you know why? Because first 100 pages of this book gave me an urge to perform hara-kiri by using my kindle. I even found myself murmuring Japanese words ( Only Japanese words I know: the menu of my favorite sushi place, so this book made me achieve something impossible!)<br /><br />So if you know my address, you can stop by for throwing rotten tomatoes, eggs and screaming “Idiot! What’s wrong with you? Aren’t you intelligent enough to understand the story?” But at first you need to pass my crazy neighbor who sings BOYZ II Men songs day and night. (I’m not exaggerating, yesterday I woke up with his singing “End of the road” in the most ear bleeding tune!)<br /><br />I read too many good reviews and I truly love this author’s works and this is at the top of my most anticipated books of this year! So as soon as I get my hands on it, I jumped up down, danced, yelled, and somersaulted. As a summary I did all those mature things a regular 40 years old crazy lady could perform!<br /><br />But as soon as I started to read, I thought that something wrong with me because I felt like I disconnected with the book as if somebody pulled off my plug or turned my brain cells’ functioning off. I felt like Jim Carrey from Dumb and Dumber, giving blank looks to the walls as my saliva is dripping down on my chin! So I read first 100 pages at 5 hours. Can you believe it? You cannot! But it’s true! And I didn’t totally get anything. So I gave short breaks, popped up my fish oil tablets (I thought they could help my mind to function faster!)<br /><br />I kept repeating myself, “This is the same author who wrote Six of Crows, right? Maybe I’m at the alternate universe and I read different version of book or too much Chardonnay finally turned me into regular brainless Hollywood person!”<br /> So the intriguing blurb of Galaxy Stern a.k.a Alex who suffered from big traumas, abuse, too many horrible things finally makes a fresh start by starting to study in Yale. She meets with Darlington ( definitely not my darling!) who informs her about nine secret societies and their rituals. As the season turns into spring, we see that Alex still fights with her past demons and a girl’s murder triggers her traumatic experiences. She is so adamant to solve the case even though it means she has to face the ghosts of her old life.<br /><br />So this seems like my kind of story I actually like. It’s dark! It’s wild! There is a big mystery! Magical rituals, mystery, a tormented but strong heroine!<br /><br />BUT… My expectations are flying in the sky because I know this author has one of the most talented brains on the earth. But the story telling are so slow and those intelligent references seemed like too pretentious and made me confused and lost! I pushed myself too hard to finish like a job or a secret mission but reading shouldn’t be a torture or obligation. You read it because you love the books and you love how they make you feel. But this book didn’t make me relaxed, happy, entertained, excited, it just suffocated me.<br />I couldn’t relate with Alex, Darlington and I tried my best but I didn’t like Sandow, Hellie, Dawlos, too.<br /><br />So maybe I decided to read this in a wrong time. Maybe I had a focusing problem or I’m in a dark mood when winter comes or I didn’t feel like to read something like that! But unfortunately this is not my cup of tea (I hate by the way! Let’s say not cup of my almond milk latte!)<br /><br />You may expel me to the minority city and punish me to have a few days without my kindle or boo me for my review but these are my thoughts. This book didn’t work for me!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2617472548385414234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2683207134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683207134" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683207134?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/40656322-flatiron-books">Flatiron Books</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683207134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2635000549777582154"><b>CONGRATULATIONS-Goodreads Choice Awards Adult Fantasy Winner!</b><br/><br/><i>"I am a daughter of Lethe, and the wolves are at the door."</i><br/><br/>Hello friends, and good evening. Do me a favor will you? Could you all please stand up? Thank you. Now, if you're a fan of dark fantasy/horror and stories involving occult magic, please remain standing; everyone else can sit down. Remain standing if you also retain the ability to push through a read that has a slew of triggers, such as sexual assault, graphic rape of a 12 year </span>
  <span id="freeText2635000549777582154" style="display:none"><b>CONGRATULATIONS-Goodreads Choice Awards Adult Fantasy Winner!</b><br /><br /><i>"I am a daughter of Lethe, and the wolves are at the door."</i><br /><br />Hello friends, and good evening. Do me a favor will you? Could you all please stand up? Thank you. Now, if you're a fan of dark fantasy/horror and stories involving occult magic, please remain standing; everyone else can sit down. Remain standing if you also retain the ability to push through a read that has a slew of triggers, such as sexual assault, graphic rape of a 12 year old girl, murder, gore, death, drug abuse/overdose, possession, the forced eating of excrement to a rapist, and many more subjects. Great, now also remain standing if you are ok with reading a book where you are dropped into the middle of a world much like our own, but you have no idea what's going on and have to figure it out as you go at a slow burning pace, until all is revealed. If you're still with me, follow me to the next portion; the rest of you may be excused.<br /><br /><b>Why the dramatics, Chels?</b> Well, to be fair, this book won't be for everyone. I'll go as far as saying that it won't be for a majority of people. <i>Ninth House</i> is an extremely dark and heavy read, one that is well-written and plotted, but contains many aspects that are so niche that I can't imagine a majority of Bardugo's YA fantasy fans crossing over into this realm. Many of my close, trusted friends have struggled with this book, and I highly respect their opinions and reasons for not resonating with it, and if you're looking for a wonderful, objective 3 star review to offset mine, I suggest you read Melanie's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343881211?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.<br /><br /><b>If you're still with me, I'd like to take a moment and break down, into sections, just what ground the book covers. There will be no major spoilers, but if you want to go in blind without any sense of what the book is about, stop here. </b><br /><br /><i>"That was what magic did. It revealed the heart of who you'd been before life took away your belief in the possible. It gave back the world all lonely children longed for. That was what Lethe had done for him. Maybe it could do that for Alex as well."</i><br /><br />The book opens with a touch of an ending, and abruptly brings us back to what I will refer to as Present Day. We are dropped directly into Alex's daily schedule, and over the course of the first 150 pages or so, we slowly gather information on the various secret societies at Yale, how magic is involved, and snippets of Alex's past that lead her to Yale in the first place. This is the section where the book weeds out those who bought this because it's one of the most popular new releases of 2019, and those who are genuinely interested in dark ADULT fantasy. Once we get a general sense of this alternate contemporary world, we realize there are two mysteries at hand. One is the murder of a local and there appears to have been magic involved. Who killed her and for what purpose? This particular mystery does tie into the next mystery I'll be mentioning, but suffice it to say that this murder is solved and completely wrapped up in this first installment. The second mystery is the disappearance of Alex's mentor, Darlington. This mystery receives answers but will continue on into the sequel. Along the way, Alex teams up with a few human people and also Grays (spirits of the deceased that still roam the earth) to solve both mysteries, while also revealing the entirety of Alex's background and how she came to be at Yale. <br /><br />I'll be honest, I had my doubts in the beginning. When I say that the pacing is slow, I mean it is S-L-O-W. The audio version of <i>Ninth House</i> features two of my favorite narrators, and I found that this format worked best for me in the beginning, and I enjoyed it so much that I mostly listened to the entire book rather than reading my hard copy. Once the ball gets rolling, I became fully engrossed. I can't tell you how interesting it was to read about all of these real societies with the added flair of magical abilities. Bardugo created a world that felt eerily realistic; no detail is left untouched and she used the old Stephen King method of "make it real, but change the slightest detail to make it not real," and this worked beautifully. <br /><br />After a majority of the book being the slow burn, the ending is absolute bonkers in the best way! Wild, action packed, and with a few twists I did not see coming! I felt the ending was brilliant; it wasn't a cliffhanger but it did leave me ready and wanting to come back for more. I'll stop before I ramble on, but I'd like to cautiously recommend this book with gusto. If you've read it, I'd love to chat with you about it. If you decide this isn't for you, I respect that, and I can't wait for the next book we get to chat about together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2635000549777582154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2136731107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136731107" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136731107?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136731107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16128279291688658853">DNF - pg 146.<br/><br/>I actually cannot do it. I can't finish it. I wanted to like this book <i>so bad</i>, and then I just wanted to finish it so bad, but it's sending me into a serious book slump. I'm giving up.<br/><br/>After struggling through the first 100 pages, I decided to take a break, read something else, and then come back to it. Sometimes it's the timing, you know? So I went and read a good portion of Isaacson's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21856367.The_Innovators_How_a_Group_of_Hackers__Geniuses_and_Geeks_Created_the_Digital_Revolution' title='The Innovators How a Group of Hackers, Geniuses and Geeks Created the Digital Revolution by Walter Isaacson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Innovators</a>, got myself neck-deep in some quantum computing, because after reading that, some m</span>
  <span id="freeText16128279291688658853" style="display:none">DNF - pg 146.<br /><br />I actually cannot do it. I can't finish it. I wanted to like this book <i>so bad</i>, and then I just wanted to finish it so bad, but it's sending me into a serious book slump. I'm giving up.<br /><br />After struggling through the first 100 pages, I decided to take a break, read something else, and then come back to it. Sometimes it's the timing, you know? So I went and read a good portion of Isaacson's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21856367.The_Innovators_How_a_Group_of_Hackers__Geniuses_and_Geeks_Created_the_Digital_Revolution" title="The Innovators How a Group of Hackers, Geniuses and Geeks Created the Digital Revolution by Walter Isaacson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Innovators</a>, got myself neck-deep in some quantum computing, because after reading that, some magical Yale mystery has got to blow my socks off, right? But I only forced myself through another 46 pages before my eyes were glazing over and I started mentally screaming: holy shit! Please tell me again how transistors are made! Please!<br /><br />I saw a couple of people say they were hoping <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43263680.Ninth_House__Alex_Stern___1_" title="Ninth House (Alex Stern, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Ninth House</a> would be like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6101718.The_Magicians__The_Magicians___1_" title="The Magicians (The Magicians, #1) by Lev Grossman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magicians</a> and were disappointed that it wasn't, but I gotta say: I found the first 146 pages of this book to be exactly like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6101718.The_Magicians__The_Magicians___1_" title="The Magicians (The Magicians, #1) by Lev Grossman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magicians</a>. Unbelievable pretentiousness, almost constant highbrow intellectual references, nothing actually happening... If it was marketed somewhere that this book was like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6101718.The_Magicians__The_Magicians___1_" title="The Magicians (The Magicians, #1) by Lev Grossman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magicians</a>, then I completely missed that. <br /><br />I had been worried about all the promise of dark themes-- some of the trigger warnings sounded downright revolting --but I never expected Bardugo to write something so cold, aloof and boring. Normally when I don't finish a book, I ask people to spoil the ending for me, but I genuinely do not care what happens.<br /><br />If you are new to Bardugo, I still recommend checking out the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> duology. Far more gripping than this.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16128279291688658853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1793940681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1793940681" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1793940681?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473227965" href="/book/show/44140764-ninth-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=feminist-as-fuck">feminist-as-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1793940681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7137869330040820510"><i>"There were always excuses for why girls died."</i><br/><br/>To answer your question: yes, it really is <i>that</i> good.<br/><br/>Ninth House and I had a bit of a slow start. The new world that Bardugo has created might not be set in a fictional fantasy universe, but it features enough new concepts, characters, and settings that it takes some time to take it all in. Not only does every character have an alias and maybe even a nickname, so do the buildings at Yale. And since all my Yale knowledge is based on that cute little </span>
  <span id="freeText7137869330040820510" style="display:none"><i>"There were always excuses for why girls died."</i><br /><br />To answer your question: yes, it really is <i>that</i> good.<br /><br />Ninth House and I had a bit of a slow start. The new world that Bardugo has created might not be set in a fictional fantasy universe, but it features enough new concepts, characters, and settings that it takes some time to take it all in. Not only does every character have an alias and maybe even a nickname, so do the buildings at Yale. And since all my Yale knowledge is based on that cute little courtyard from Gilmore Girls, I struggled to figure out where and who and what was going on. As soon as I had grasped all of that, though, I was unable to resist the pull of this dark, compelling, murderous book.<br /><br />I don't know where to start. The book was sombre and thrilling, brimming with ancient mysteries, magic, and the promise of danger. The characters were incredibly well-painted, my favourites being Turner and Dawes. The plot was thought-out, and until the very end, it was tense and exciting. My only criticism comes with the one or other reveal during the final showdown. Bardugo dropped enough clues here and there that the reader could have figured out who might have been behind the murder at the centre of this novel. That is until the plot is twisted yet again and delivers an explanation that adds new possibilities that no reader could have suspected. It was drawn up out of thin air and therefore not as genius as I had expected it to be.<br /><br />Now, be warned. If this book is one thing, it's violent. There are some graphic scenes that show sexual abuse. There is trauma and pain and it's not glossed over. I've seen people get mad at Leigh because she chose to show these horrible acts of violence. They accused her of exploiting the pain for shock value. I cannot agree with them. The novel is deeply feminist and shows characters with a past that is tough, that made them survivors. Readers also have no right to know whether the scenes in the book are based on the author's personal experiences. She doesn't have to justify writing about sexual abuse by proving that she has been in a similar position. I do, however, agree that the book needs trigger warnings.<br /><br />I honestly can't wait for the sequel. I mean, I personally don't care about [redacted] and whether they'll manage to save them or not, but the world that Bardugo created is so rich and leaves so much to discover that I wouldn't mind another three to five books. It feels like Alex Stern only just got started kicking ass.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7137869330040820510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3011366864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011366864" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011366864?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473227965" href="/book/show/44140764-ninth-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=adult-new-adult">adult-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011366864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9552629345597308213">4.25/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/11/25/ninth-house-alex-stern-1-by-leigh-bardugo/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><b>me:</b> *seeing the whole anarchy this book has created* I wonder if I too can ruin my life<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571909072i/28343241.jpg' width='340' height='310' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh, behold the majestic weird shit that I am, reading my first Leigh Bardugo book ever! <br/><br/>YES. You may laugh at me and judge me and all that, but honestly, this book has created some serious anarchy after publication, a type of anarchy that made me stop and think: “If this book makes people feel so intense, then it is a make it or break it for me for sure”. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9552629345597308213" style="display:none">4.25/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/11/25/ninth-house-alex-stern-1-by-leigh-bardugo/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><b>me:</b> *seeing the whole anarchy this book has created* I wonder if I too can ruin my life<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571909072i/28343241.jpg" width="340" height="310" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, behold the majestic weird shit that I am, reading my first Leigh Bardugo book ever! <br><br>YES. You may laugh at me and judge me and all that, but honestly, this book has created some serious anarchy after publication, a type of anarchy that made me stop and think: “If this book makes people feel so intense, then it is a make it or break it for me for sure”. This book was about to be the ultimate answer to my eternal question – “Will I ever even like Leigh Bardugo?” <br><br>The answer to that lame question – <i>Yes</i>. And I know that’s not even one of her greatest works.<br><br><i>
  <b>Ninth House</b>
</i> was and is (at least for me) a weird combination of delightful and crafty action, disgusting and unnecessary details and a perpetual feeling of cringe. But <b>I bloody loved it</b> <s>and that shows how much of next-level trash I can be.</s><br><br><b>THERE IS NO YOUNG ADULT CONTENT HERE.</b> And I mean it. For those who don’t really get along with (new) adult content, please put the book away or suck it up and read it on your own expense. <br><br><b>Disclaimer</b>: it contains emotional triggers such as child molesting, alcohol and drug abuse, physical and psychical abuse, curse words, violence and other things in that particular area.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Mors <s>vincit</s> irrumat omnia.”</b>
</i><br><br>To be completely honest, I don’t know much about Yale and its organisational system or its secret societies or whatever voodoo is happening there at the moment. And even more honest, I don’t quite care. But bringing this topic in discussion and making a somehow “magical” experience out of it is quite interesting.<br><br>This society, Lethe, is there to supervise every abuse of magic the other eight secret societies are conducting. In reality, Lethe is a mess and they barely have a bloody idea what they are doing there, but you know, I’ve been to my current faculty for three years now and I have no idea what I’m doing either so Lethe, I got you bruh. <br><br>The action here seems to be purely symbolic in my opinion. I mean, things don’t really happen until the last 150 pages whatsoever. But the interesting thing is that when the whole mystery started to unravel, it kind of caught you off guard. I, for instance, was caught off guard by the whole ending and this hurts the Agatha Christie fan in me because it is literally a very easy-to-solve mystery.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567689008ra/28103776.gif" width="449" height="241" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, let’s talk about my favourite part: <b>Darlington</b>.<br><br>Daniel Arlington aka Darlington is the so-called “gentleman of Lethe” and oh, doesn’t this world need more gentlemen? For real now, that’s an honest question. <br><br>Everyone loves Darlington. And I do too. And you’ll do too. I cannot explain that, but he’s got a sort of magnetic personality that fascinates everyone. He’s like the biggest geek on the planet meets the rich, upper-class boy meets the charismatic boy next door. He’s all that and he’s <b>precious.</b><br><br>Galaxy Stern, a culturally ambiguous girl with a long record at the ready and a very comical but interesting name is not immune to Darlington’s charms. In fact, she might be as in love with him as the rest of us. <br><br>Alex sees ghosts. And she has been seeing them for all her life. Which is kind of disturbing? She was bullied for it and she became a broken girl. All that rebellion was purely a defence mechanism gone wrong. But after all, when life gives you sour lemons like that you have to make a sour lemonade and to try to sweeten it with everything you have at hand. Or to drink it as it is. <br><br> <i>
  <b>“We all have spaces we keep blank.”</b>
</i><br><br>I am not very fond of Alex’s character just yet, she’s indeed a hard girl to love but I think she might grow on me after a while. I already love her wits so I just need another push to be sure I like her. <br><br>On the other hand, another great character of this book is Pamela Dawes whom I actually really love. Pammie is the mum-friend and there’s no way you’ll argue that after you come to know her. Hell, I’ll let her cook some lemon chicken soup for me anytime, that’s how amazing I think she is.<br><br>There’s a lot going on in this book. It is something hard to get into because the beginning is extremely confusing. The action is quite slow and not necessarily that complex, but somehow, until the end, there is something there. Something that leaves you thinking that you actually enjoy it. <br><br>It’s a complicated book to like, to be honest. But it has charm. There is something dark that keeps moving, twisting and turning.<br><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/8751594b-a7aa-4b31-bf4e-a7e24febf75d_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-inspired</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9552629345597308213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2927638778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2927638778" />
    <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments"><img alt="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554228831p2/67920559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2927638778?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=fantasy-me-up">fantasy-me-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=most-anticipated">most-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=darker-than-my-soul">darker-than-my-soul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=unlikeable-characters">unlikeable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=what-the-actual-fuck">what-the-actual-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2927638778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10551795004664063339"><i>
  <b>"That was what magic did. It revealed the heart of who you’d been before life took away your belief in the possible. It gave back the world all lonely children longed for. "</b>
</i> <br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573635317i/28442998._SY540_.jpg' width='700' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><a href='https://phantomrin.tumblr.com/post/188453982720/day-18-queen-mab-alex-stern-from-ninth-house' rel='nofollow noopener'>©</a><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1565175686i/27951313._SX540_.jpg' width='600' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>-dnf @30%-</b><br/>I don't think I have ever been more disappointed in myself for not being able to love this book. Leigh Bardugo continues to be my queen of fantasy, this one was just a complete and utter miss for me. <br/>_______________ <br/><br/><u>
  <b>*all the sighs*</b>
</u><br/>I'm still not certain that this review will get all my thoughts across. I'</span>
  <span id="freeText10551795004664063339" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"That was what magic did. It revealed the heart of who you’d been before life took away your belief in the possible. It gave back the world all lonely children longed for. "</b>
</i> <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573635317i/28442998._SY540_.jpg" width="700" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="https://phantomrin.tumblr.com/post/188453982720/day-18-queen-mab-alex-stern-from-ninth-house" rel="nofollow noopener">©</a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1565175686i/27951313._SX540_.jpg" width="600" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>-dnf @30%-</b><br>I don't think I have ever been more disappointed in myself for not being able to love this book. Leigh Bardugo continues to be my queen of fantasy, this one was just a complete and utter miss for me. <br>_______________ <br><br><u>
  <b>*all the sighs*</b>
</u><br>I'm still not certain that this review will get all my thoughts across. I'm also very blatantly stating this now... because I DNFed this book, this review isn't going to be able to provide any summaries, commentaries etc etc. It's partially why I didn't give it a rating; firstly because I couldn't even get halfway and secondly, because I think I might return to <i>Ninth House</i> at a future date. I want to give this book more of a chance but as it stands now, this was not for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573779433ra/28451497.gif" width="600" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I've read a lot of people opinions on how it gets better and I'm holding on to that for the next time I try. A caveat though; this book and everything about it (aside from it being Fantasy) really shouldn't be compared to the Grishaverse or Leigh's previous books. They are intended for two different types of demographics and <i>Ninth House</i> deals with some very heavy "adult" themes. <br><br>To start things off (very bluntly), I got bored. There was nothing that kept me turning the pages other than self-determination and it came to a point where even that wasn't enough. I was doing that thing where you read a paragraph and then read it again (3 times) because you realize you weren't paying any attention at all...I found the pacing in this book to be excruciatingly slow. Nothing significant enough was happening that had me at the edge and the "mysterious" elements didn't hold enough suspense or warrant excitement from me. Again, this opinion is simply my own and it might have been a fact of picking this book at the wrong time.<br><br>Another key thing I noticed that caused <i>-several-</i> naps whilst reading was the writing style. The writing in this book is very narrative, and while it's not without merit, it simply didn't captivate me. I felt like it was telling me, rather than showing me and I craved for emotional description from the characters. Which leads me to another note...I got really weary of Darlington. This is going to be very problematic because A LOT of people place him as the winning character of this book. Still, I found myself leaning towards wanting Alex's chapters more than his. Nothing about Darlington made me anticipate meeting him...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566305247ra/28021611.gif" width="600" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There were way too many infor-dumps and if I had to sum up my reading experience, it would be a quote directly from this book: <br><i>
  <b>"You start out excited, and by page two you realize it’s all a lot of words and not much drama."</b>
</i> When I saw that, I felt like I was being called out to be honest (drama in this case meaning something actually, yknow... HaPpEnIng). I needed to stop reading before it put me in a slump, so I did. On another note though, Amazon Studios is going to <a href="https://deadline.com/2019/10/grishaverse-authorleigh-bardugo-ninth-house-amazon-studios-tv-series-development-1202756743/" rel="nofollow noopener">develop this into a series</a> and THAT, I'm looking forward to. It might just push me to read it before I watch it! <br><br>Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12772859-mischas" rel="nofollow noopener">this cutie</a> although, I don't really know if it counts because she's being a trooper and still reading and I'm now just waving the moral support flag. <br><br><br><u>
  <b>pre-review</b>
</u><br><b>do i have a considerable amount of books that i already need to read? would i drop (quote me on this) <i>everything</i> for this? if leigh bardugo wrote a 100,000 word essay on the growing strategies of cacti, would i also do the same?</b> yes, yes and also yes. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565176073ra/27951383.gif" width="600" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br><i>"By the time Alex managed to get the blood out of her good wool coat, it was too warm to wear it. Spring had come on grudgingly; pale-blue mornings failed to deepen, turning instead to moist, sullen afternoons, and stubborn frost lined the road in high, dirty meringues....<br>....That was in the spring. But the trouble had begun on a night in the full dark of winter, when Tara Hutchins died and Alex still thought she might get away with everything."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10551795004664063339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2857519146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2857519146" />
    <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling"><img alt="• Lindsey Dahling •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578858809p2/26262267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2857519146?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lindsey Dahling •" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling">• Lindsey Dahling •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2857519146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13397527028705430841">I should start this by saying had anyone other than Queen Leigh Bardugo written this, I would have given it 1 star. There's also a 90% chance this would be on my DNF shelf.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Things I liked:</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>1. Darlington</b><br/>He was the most likable character in the book for me, but even he fell flat. I get it, Dar. You love the big old mansion you inherited. What else do you have going for you? (Jury is still out on that one.)<br/><br/><b>2. ....................</b><br/><br/>Welp. I've just realized that I liked literally nothing else about t</span>
  <span id="freeText13397527028705430841" style="display:none">I should start this by saying had anyone other than Queen Leigh Bardugo written this, I would have given it 1 star. There's also a 90% chance this would be on my DNF shelf.<br><br><b>
  <u>Things I liked:</u>
</b><br><br><b>1. Darlington</b><br>He was the most likable character in the book for me, but even he fell flat. I get it, Dar. You love the big old mansion you inherited. What else do you have going for you? (Jury is still out on that one.)<br><br><b>2. ....................</b><br><br>Welp. I've just realized that I liked literally nothing else about the book.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>It's a no from me:</u>
</b><br><br><b>1. There's barely any dialogue. </b><br> I don't get it. Bardugo is a master at writing witty dialogue. SHE'S A DAMN PRO. Unfortunately, it hardly makes an appearance in <i>Ninth House</i>. Honestly, the real mystery of this "mystery" book is figuring out why the hell her editor would let her publish something that's 90% narration.<br><br><b>2. SERIOUSLY. SO MUCH NARRATION.</b><br>I really don't need the history behind each and every secret society house. I don't care about the exact layout of Yale's campus. Don't care about what Alex is wearing. Don't care about visiting the library for the 800th time just for Alex to learn nothing. I couldn't even care about all of the graphic stuff that people posted trigger warnings for left and right because it all fell flat. It seemed sort of rushed and pointless and I never cared that any of it was happening because she did that whole amateur TELL, not SHOW your freshman Creative Writing teachers instruct you not to do.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571700871ra/28331877.gif" alt="giphy-3" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3. The graphic stuff felt pointless.</b><br>Honestly, it felt more gratuitous than anything. Did adding those elements really develop the characters? No. Not really. Alex Stern is the victim of horrendous trauma, and yet she still read quite vanilla to me. So then what was the point of detailing that trauma? (Jury is out on that one, too.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571700641ra/28331865.gif" alt="giphy-1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4. IT WAS SO DAMN LONG.</b><br>WHY? WHYYYYYYY? I kept having to go back and reread paragraphs/pages because I'd realize that ONCE AGAIN my eyes had completely glazed over BECAUSE NOTHING WAS HAPPENING. And when something did happen...<br><br><b>5. ...IT WAS COMPLETELY FUCKING RUSHED.</b><br>I'm not exaggerating when I say the book will go on and on for several chapters without anything happening other than Alex walking around and the omniscient narrator telling us she hasn't slept in awhile. Then, SUDDENLY, Alex would have some random epiphany, she'd run out to investigate, would be completely right about 100% of her suspicions, and then it would go back to chapters of nothing. The end was even more rushed because everything was revealed/solved within a whole two chapters. THE BOOK IS 450 PAGES. YET IT TAKES TWO WHOLE CHAPTERS FOR PERFECT ALEX TO FIGURE IT OUT AND UNMASK THE VILLAIN. If I wanted to watch Scooby Doo, for both the repetition and the reveal, I WOULD TURN ON THE FUCKING TV.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571700083ra/28331796.gif" alt="tenor" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ahem. Sorry. Sorry. Going back to being objective and rational now.<br><br>Eh, forget it. I'm too worked up. Maybe I'll finish this review later, but probably not BECAUSE MY BLOOD PRESSURE CANNOT HANDLE IT.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571701397ra/28331893.gif" alt="louie-storm-out" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still love you, Leigh. I just need you to...not do this again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13397527028705430841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
